< Review>
My puppy, ruthie, boots straight to them when we get there. So it makes me feel good about leaving her for the day. I check her after every pickup and there has not been an issue for me.

We've been here about 4 or 5 times now and have only done the Doggy daycare. Price has been straight forward for us everytime. I think it's the same amount to other doggy daycares in the area.

I have never gotten a card with ruthie's "report card" during any of my visits...I've seen people get them though so they do make a card haha which I was initially excited about because she hadn't ever been to a daycare before.

<Rating>5</Rating><Review>Perfection. These guys are all about getting it perfect. When my nearly new (just over 10,000 miles!) 4WD Chevy Tahoe Premier got rear-ended by a careless kid I was heartsick, believing it could never be returned to the new-shiny-solid we loved. One of the most sophisticated and complex vehicles Chevy makes, our Tahoe is absolutely loaded with every kind of computer-controlled, super-sensing device GM makes. And it's got extra towing muscle with it's large V-8 engine and full towing package to pull our RV.  What's more, our special-ordered paint (tri-color, pearlescent white) makes it beautiful to behold... but a very difficult paint-matching repair job!  Given all this complexity, I assumed that it would be nearly impossible to return to its near-new condition.

But the folks at E3 are a tenacious lot. They inspected and measured and ordered parts and repaired and worked with two Chevy dealers on some of the mechanical stuff (sometimes rejecting the dealer's work and insisting it be done over!). They were picky, inspecting and re-inspecting and not afraid to stop and order an obscure, deeply buried part that had minor damage and which might have been ignored because no one would ever notice it was broken. In short, they were aggressive and acted as our advocates with the insurance company and the dealer repair people throughout the entire repair process. Yes, it took a long time. But they essentially rebuilt our beautiful vehicle to their exacting standards. And what we got back was a is a Tahoe Premier that is just like new.

I highly recommed this family operation. 118022695685207467339</user_id>
<Name>Dexter Dean<//Name><Date>1577632138366<//Date><rating>4<//rating>< Text>
Shihlin Taiwan Street Snacks is a chain with three locations in the Bay Area and the multiple locations are a clear sign that there's a demand in the Bay Area for street eats: affordable, authentic, local cuisine that is quick and tasty to eat.

Having visited Taiwan to try the night markets (of which the one in Shihlin is one of the most famous), I had high hopes stopping by here for a quick snack.  The menu is on point with the XXL Chicken and the popcorn chicken being the most representative.  Other options include oyster noodles, braised chicken rice and plum fries.  Prices (for the Bay Area) are reasonable at under $10.  Our orders:

Grapefruit Tea - $3.79.  refreshing and not too sweet.  Pairs well with the fried food

XXL Chicken - $8.95.  Available either as white meat or thigh and breast, the portion size is generous and the texture crispy and juicy. The seasoning is good and has a slight kick at the end.

Brown Sugar Fresh Boba Tea - $4.79.  Brown sugar is the latest rage and the version here is decent.  The fresh boba could have been better but the flavor of the brown sugar is good without being  too sweet.

Overall, quite happy to have a Shihlin Taiwan snacks in the area.  It seems to be our go to quick spot in the area and the service is quick and friendly.  We could use a location in the South Bay.

Shihlin accepts credit cards including American Express.< /Text>

< review>
Small kiosk starbucks in the center of the Faahion Fair Mall.  They have a tiny selection of prepackaged coffee, mugs & other retail items.  Very limited seating.  Dont expect to find a seat.  Unfortunately other Mall shoppers take advantage of the Starbucks seating leaving Starbucks customers no where to sit. Within the last year with the change in management this Starbucks has gone from a 5 star rating to a 2 star. There has been a complete shift in the quality of customer service, cleanliness, quickness, quality of drinks, and the overall experience ever since management has changed. Me and my colleagues have been frequenting this location for The Last 5 Years that used to be our favorite spot. The staff was friendly personable warm and always greeted us with a friendly attitude. They took good care of the regulars and appreciated loyalty. The new group of Staff seems bitter annoyed and unhappy to be there and that reflects in the quality of their drinks the speed in which the drinks are prepared and the overall experience. It's understandable that this location is busy being in the middle of the mall, however, thats not a good reason to skimp on service.   A couple of really good staff members still work behind the counter however unfortunately they are overshadowed by the negative ones. Don't bother coming in on a busy weekend you should expect to wait 20 to 25 minutes for your drink.<//review>

< Review>
There are a lot of trails you can enjoy. Great place for hiking, running, mountain biking and horseback riding. Some parts of the trails are steep, like the first half of Joice trail starting at Benal ranch, again Joice trail coming up from the east to Vista loop trail, Boundary trail near the Coyote Peak and the first half of Mine trail at Nored ranch . If you want thrill of MTB'ing, try the rocky ridge trail. Most of the trails have no shade, so you need sunscreen and lots of water. Sometimes you can see snakes, wild turkeys, dears along the trail. A couple of months ago, I spotted a group of wild boars.</Review>

< Text>
This is a great safe place to go hiking. If you have a dog you are able to bring them as long as they are on a leash. Luckily every Trail is easy to find and even easier to find your way back. The bathrooms are super clean and they are always stocked with paper towels, toilet paper, and hand soap. Last time I went the meter to charge for parking was down but keep in mind that you should have cash on you just in case the ticket meter is working again. Last time I checked used to be $6.<//Text>

< Review>
Well this time I was in the Southern part of the park, and it is not nearly as pleasant as the Northern part that you enter and pay a parking fee. Unfortunately, a lot of people come here to drink and smoke marijuana in their cars and they discard bottles on the ground. Be careful because there is a lot of broken glass and trash here. The Northern entrance is much, much better and has easy access to trails and has benches and nice trees to sit under. Go to the Northern entrance, yeah.</Review>

< text>
Absolutely amazing county park in the heart of Silicon Valley with a diverse network of trails overseeing the valley and adjoining Santa Teresa Golf Course. This park is incredibly accessible for most San Jose residents via Bernal Road and is a great way to get back to nature and escape the everyday hustle and bustle of city life. The trail up to Coyote Peak is quite challenging but offers those who make it to the top a majestic view all the way to San Francisco on a clear day. One of my favorite Bay Area parks by far.</text>

<Date>1575559152404<//Date><Rate>5< /Rate><Text>I lived with in walking distance to this park, I was able to find parking outside the park, sometimes it gets busy and you would have to park at the curb.
It would take me about 1.5 hours to do my usual hike. You will find small deer, turkeys, boars, quale, rattle snakes, etc.
At the entrance they have a spot with a map and information about the type of wild animals you can encounter. They have pamphlets that come with a map and information you can take.
They also provide hiking sticks it's a first come first serve.
I would totally recommend it!</Text>< Pics>

This park is a nice place to go hiking and mountain biking. Sometimes you will see deer, turkey, or quail around this area. There many also be snakes on the trail. Be careful as they may attack you if you get too close. I try to leave a good distance when walking past them. They will simply slither away if you do so. In the spring, there is a variety of different wildflowers. Sometimes the flowers will be in big patches. Sometimes there will be nice sunsets in the park also.</text>

< name>
Marco Paganini<//name>
< date>
1461389869308</date>
<rate>5< /rate><review>Santa Teresa is my favorite park in San Jose. The park occupies a sizable area and has a fair amount of trails for hikers, bikers, and horse riders. The highest point in the park (Coyote Peak) offers a nice view of San Jose (but be prepared for the steep climb, especially if you're biking there.)

Santa Teresa is usually not very crowded, even on weekends. Weekdays are especially nice for those who enjoy activities like animal and bird watching, or a lone bike ride.

Unlike many other parks, leashed dogs *are* allowed here (but please, make sure your dog is on a leash!).The park also offers (clean) public restrooms and a large covered area which can be reserved for parties.

For mountain bikers, the park offers a wide range of biking trails, ranging from almost flat and easy to rocky and technical. No matter how experienced you are, you can always create a route that will get you entertained (and tired).

The only thing I miss in this park is a large body of water. There are a few seasonal streams running through the park, but no lakes.

The parking lot is fairly large, and parking was $6 last time I checked. Rangers do check the place and will give you tickets if you don't pay the parking fees or park your car on the road.< /review><pictures>None< /pictures><response>None<//response>< GmapID>
0x808e2fc181066781:0xc7069f6213d5dbba< /GmapID>

<Text>(Translated by Google) Come to Santa Teresa County Park, located ten miles south of downtown San Jose in the Santa Teresa Mountains. This 1,673-acre park has a rich history and spectacular views from the trails above the Almaden and Santa Clara valleys. The secluded highland valley of the park provides a quiet episode for exploring the natural surroundings of the surrounding developed areas. Santa Teresa County Park is located at the southern end of Santa Teresa. The park can be accessed from the Alma Mountain Valley or Santa Clara Valley. From the Santa Clara Valley, take the US 101 or 85 motorway to the Bernal Road exit. Drive 1.3 miles west along Bernal Road and cross Santa Teresa Avenue to Santa Teresa. Bernal Road continues through the park's Santa Teresa Golf Club and enters the hills. Located on Bernal Road, Pueblo Day Use Area is set in a small open valley on a hill.
